Saturday, 12:30 p.m. – Sealed Deck Building Exercise #1: The Pool
-----------------------------------------------------------------


*by Noel Neo*

 

Below is one of the Sealed pools that an unnamed pro received today. What do you think the pro went with?


Would it be the Azorius deck backed by [Sphinx of the Chimes](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sphinx+of+the+Chimes), [New Prahv Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=New+Prahv+Guildmage), and a trio of detainers, or would he lean to red for [Chaos Imps](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chaos+Imps) and [Utvara Hellkite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Utvara+Hellkite)? Then there's the suite of removal available with black, including Assassin's Strike, [Ultimate Price](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ultimate+Price), and twin [Auger Spree](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Auger+Spree).


Let us know what you think is the best option with this pool on the forums, and check back later today to find out what our pro went with!


 [![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/magic/sealeddeckbuilder/assets/Frontloader-Preview.jpg)](http://www.wizards.com/magic/sealeddeckbuilder/index.html?draftid=gpsin13a)
[![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/activity/sealedDeckBuilderButton_Static.jpg)](http://www.wizards.com/magic/sealeddeckbuilder/index.html?draftid=gpsin13a)


Saturday, 1:15 p.m. – State Of The Format, with Nicholas Wong
-------------------------------------------------------------


*by Pip Foweraker*

 

I caught up with old-school observer Nicholas Wong for a quick chat about how the *Return to Ravnica* format has played out over time. With *Gatecrash* just around the corner and previews popping up all over the Internet, now is a good time to look at where we've been.


*Return to Ravnica* is one of the most popular sets in **Magic**'s history. Thousands upon thousands of drafts have shaped the format from its early inception. Wong, a keen drafter, has observed a maturation of the format over time. "Players are starting to realise that there are decent enchantments out there, whereas in the early format, you hardly saw any," Wong says. "Enchantment removal is starting to see play, and [Keening Apparition](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Keening+Apparition) is slowly gaining value."




|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| 
Keening Apparition
 | 
Stab Wound
 |
| 
Knightly Valor
 |

As for the Sealed format, Wong points out that it's fairly easy to make a 'decent' deck: the number of playables in the format means you'll always make your 23 – so the skill becomes finding the best possible deck, with each card decision weighing heavily. Sealed decks are less focused than draft, and balancing out power and consistency is a key challenge for deckbuilders.


Turning our attention to draft, the high number of playable cards in the format means, again, you're likely to not be scraping the barrel for your final picks. This forgiving draft format means that to rise against the competition, you will need to rely on skill rather than raw card power to get you there.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpsin13/GPSing-Interview-Wong.jpg) *Wong's preference for arcane trickery has paid off in many Return to Ravnica drafts.* 
As far as archetypes go, Wong's favourite is a well-drafted Izzet deck, which he says is increasingly hard to come by in draft, often reverting to his second preference of Golgari. Izzet's tactical flexibility and efficiency is what puts it over the top for Wong, [Teleportal](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Teleportal) being a flagship card that is widely respected amongst drafters for its ability to end games out of nowhere.


What have we got to look forward to? Although the archetypes have remained fairly constant throughout the *Return to Ravnica* season, Wong anticipates significant changes coming with *Gatecrash*'s release. Allied and enemy colour pairs have all been played before in draft, but perhaps not as streamlined as what we might expect nowadays. How will Simic and Orzhov combine with Golgari and Azorius?


*Gatecrash* promos are everywhere, and the introduction of the remaining 5 guilds will open up the format significantly. How will drafting strategies adapt? What cards from *Return to Ravnica* will gain or lose value in the new format? What new cards will emerge to influence the format? Keep tuned in to magicthegathering.com for daily previews, and don't forget to find a [prerelease near you](http://www.wizards.com/Magic/TCG/Events.aspx?x=mtgcom/events/prerelease-facts%20)!

Round 3 Feature Match – Choo Yong Han vs. Ng Soon Lye
-----------------------------------------------------


*by Noel Neo*

 

Yong Han is one of Singapore's finest, having made the Top 8 of Pro Tour Hollywood in 2008, and with multiple Grand Prix Top 8s and a National Championship title under his belt. He is facing off with Soon Lye, a fixture on the competitive scene locally and all round nice guy.


Long time friends, Yong Han and Soon Lye made some friendly banter about how bad their decks were as they shuffled up. Soon Lye also pulled out his special cap for hiding his golden mane during feature matches. The atmosphere got more serious as Yong Han won the die roll and opted to play.


Game 1
------


[Vassal Soul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vassal+Soul) was the MVP for Yong Han as [Centaur Healer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur+Healer) locked up the ground and Soon Lye had neither a means of putting away the flyer nor of breaking through on the ground. Soon Lye's crew of two power or less creatures could only look on helplessly as [Vassal Soul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vassal+Soul) cruised over again and again.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpsin13/Soon-Lye-considering-his-sideboard.jpg) *Soon Lye considering his sideboard.* 
Game 2
------


Soon Lye's turn to win the battle for the skies as he quickly took the game with [Daggerdrome Imp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daggerdrome+Imp) and [Zanikev Locust](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zanikev+Locust).


Yong Han might have stood a better chance had he not made the tempo play of blocking an unleashed [Grim Roustabout](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grim+Roustabout) with [Seller of Songbirds](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Seller+of+Songbirds) and its token. This play was made on turn four, after [Daggerdrome Imp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daggerdrome+Imp) had hit play, but before [Zanikev Locust](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zanikev+Locust).


Soon Lye also had an out for [Vitu-Ghazi Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vitu-Ghazi+Guildmage) in [Auger Spree](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Auger+Spree); and by the time Yong Han cracked [Grove of the Guardian](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grove+of+the+Guardian), [Explosive Impact](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Explosive+Impact) was sufficient to bring him into lethal range the next combat step.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpsin13/Yong-Han-a-cool-customer.jpg) *Yong Han - A cool customer.* 
Game 3
------


The final game was a more interesting interplay of threats and responses, starting with Yong Han's turn two [Drudge Beetle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Drudge+Beetle) getting overmatched by an unleashed [Dead Reveler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dead+Reveler) from Soon Lye. Soon Lye built on his advantage with [Viashino Racketeer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Viashino+Racketeer) (discarding [Terrus Wurm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Terrus+Wurm)), but was soon facing the prospect of a monstrous 8/8 as Yong Han laid [Grove of the Guardian](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grove+of+the+Guardian) and played [Seller of Songbirds](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Seller+of+Songbirds).


Not that the game came down to [Grove of the Guardian](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grove+of+the+Guardian), however, as Soon Lye's [Rakdos, Lord of Riots](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rakdos%2C+Lord+of+Riots) fed [Trostani's Judgment](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trostani%27s+Judgment) (getting Yong Han a Bird token) and [Collective Blessing](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Collective+Blessing) sealed the game.


**Final score: Yong Han 2 – Soon Lye 1**

Saturday, 3:05 p.m. – Sealed Deck Building Exercise #1: The Deck
----------------------------------------------------------------


*by Noel Neo*

 

Earlier today, we showed you a sealed pool that one of our unnamed pros had to work with. Featuring a choice between strong Azorius cards like [Sphinx of the Chimes](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sphinx+of+the+Chimes), [New Prahv Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=New+Prahv+Guildmage), and a trio of detainers; red for [Chaos Imps](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chaos+Imps) and [Utvara Hellkite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Utvara+Hellkite); and [Assassin's Strike](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Assassin%27s+Strike), [Ultimate Price](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ultimate+Price), and twin [Auger Spree](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Auger+Spree) with black; the pro could do well with a variety of strategies.


Our pro decided to go with removal heavy Rakdos. Have a look at his configuration and see if you agree!

Would this deck be enough to get the pro though Day 1 of Grand Prix Singapore? Check back at the end of the day as we reveal this unnamed player's identity, and how this person did!




Round 4 Feature Match – Tomoharu Saito vs. Hiroki Takeda
--------------------------------------------------------


*by Pip Foweraker*

 

Both players sat down and started chatting about their day in Japanese. With my ability to converse in their language strictly limited to ordering beers and asking directions, you'll have to miss out on any back-and-forth banter the two may enjoy.


With a chorus of 'keepu', Takeda led the game with a [Daggerdrome Imp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daggerdrome+Imp), while Saito had a [Gatecreeper Vine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gatecreeper+Vine) to smooth out his draws. Takeda summoned a [Corpsejack Menace](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Corpsejack+Menace). Saito had a [Stab Wound](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stab+Wound)s for the Imp, and a [Street Spasm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Street+Spasm) for the Menace. Takeda had a [Towering Indrik](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Towering+Indrik) and a [Golgari Longlegs](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Golgari+Longlegs) to keep up the pressure.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpsin13/GPSing-R4-Saito.jpg) *TSaito smashes Takeda's creatures.* 
Saito was unfazed, casting his third straight piece of removal: an [Assassin's Strike](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Assassin%27s+Strike) took out the Longlegs. Saito found a [Dark Revenant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Revenant), but Takeda had an [Ultimate Price](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ultimate+Price) to pop it back onto Saito's library. Saito pulled a face – the other cards in his deck were much better than the waiting [Revenant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Revenant). Takeda didn't give him a chance to find them, though: a [Rites of Reaping](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rites+of+Reaping) left the board lopsided enough that Saito went to his sideboard.


Hiroki Takeda 1 – Tomoharu Saito 0


Takeda led the action with an unleashed [Grim Roustabout](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grim+Roustabout). Saito summoned a [Vassal Soul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vassal+Soul) and passed, Takeda casting a [Golgari Keyrune](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Golgari+Keyrune). Saito's [Vassal Soul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vassal+Soul) sailed in, and he summoned a [Seller of Songbirds](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Seller+of+Songbirds) to bolster his army. Takeda's Roustabout crashed in regardless and Saito declined to block. A [Towering Indrik](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Towering+Indrik) looked to slow Saito down, but an [Arrest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arrest) took care of that.


A [Perilous Shadow](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Perilous+Shadow) for Takeda threatened to get 'all up' in Saito's 'grill' (I assume this is what was said), but Saito seemed unfazed. After a minute's thought, he cast an [Ethereal Armor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ethereal+Armor) on his Bird token and attacked with his fliers. Takeda animated his Keyrune and attacked. Saito had an [Azorius Charm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Azorius+Charm) to fend off the Keyrune for a turn, but Takeda took his opportunity to summon a [Corpsejack Menace](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Corpsejack+Menace). Saito had a [Street Spasm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Street+Spasm) to take out the Menace, and once Takeda had done the math, the pair moved on to a decider.


Tomoharu Saito 1 - Hiroki Takeda 1


A pair of mulligans for both players was followed by another for Takeda, both players starting the game down on resources. Takeda led off once again with his Roustabout. Saito kept pace with a [Keening Apparition](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Keening+Apparition) and a [Vassal Soul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vassal+Soul). Takeda summoned a [Perilous Shadow](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Perilous+Shadow), while Saito had an [Azorius Arrester](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Azorius+Arrester) to keep the pressure on.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpsin13/GPSing-R4-Takeda.jpg) *Takeda's all about the Roustabout.* 
Takeda summoned an [Axebane Guardian](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Axebane+Guardian) to shore up his defence. The early game's aggression stalled, Saito sat back and considered his options. Saito [Arrest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arrest)ed the Shadow and Takeda's Guardian blocked the [Arrest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arrest)er, the [Vassal Soul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vassal+Soul) swinging in unhindered.


Takeda attacked with his Roustabout but otherwise had no action, letting Saito attack in the same formation as before. A [Launch Party](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Launch+Party) from Takeda took out the [Vassal Soul](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vassal+Soul). Post-combat, Saito summoned a [Seller of Songbirds](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Seller+of+Songbirds), while Takeda had a [Rix Maadi Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rix+Maadi+Guildmage) to keep pace.


Saito attacked with his team once more, keen to finish off Takeda before his mage came online. Takeda traded his Guildmage for the [Keening Apparition](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Keening+Apparition), falling to perilously low life. A [Sluiceway Scorpion](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sluiceway+Scorpion) was met with a [Trostani's Judgment](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trostani%27s+Judgment), the two Bird tokens flying in before an [Explosive Impact](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Explosive+Impact) sealed the deal.


**Tomoharu Saito 2 – Hiroki Takeda 1**




Round 5 Feature Match – Calvin Ong vs. Ding Leong
-------------------------------------------------


*by Pip Foweraker*

 

Ong rapidly took control of Game 1 with a [Rix Maadi Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rix+Maadi+Guildmage) and a [Mercurial Chemister](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mercurial+Chemister). Leong's [Korozda Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Korozda+Guildmage) got Struck by an Assassin, but he quickly rebuilt with a [Golgari Longlegs](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Golgari+Longlegs) and a [Towering Indrik](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Towering+Indrik). A [Voidwielder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Voidwielder) from Ong slowed him down but briefly.


Ong took advantage of his Chemister and a [Thoughtflare](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtflare) to fill his hand with goodies. An [Ogre Jailbreaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ogre+Jailbreaker) and a [Daggerdrome Imp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daggerdrome+Imp) hit the board, leaving Leong to catch up with a [Rix Maadi Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rix+Maadi+Guildmage), a [Sluiceway Scorpion](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sluiceway+Scorpion), and a [Dryad Militant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dryad+Militant). With 7 creatures on the board, his array of men looked impressive, but Ong was outdrawing him fiercely.


With a full grip, Ong cast a [Pursuit of Knowledge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pursuit+of+Knowledge) on his [Daggerdrome Imp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daggerdrome+Imp) and attacked. Post-combat, he summoned a [Splatter Thug](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splatter+Thug) and passed. On Leong's attack, Ong used his Chemister to take out the [Rix Maadi Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rix+Maadi+Guildmage). Leong swung with his Longlegs, Militant, Scorpion, Crocodile, and Indrik. After blockers had been declared and the dust settled, Ong was left firmly ahead, with his Chemister, [Splatter Thug](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splatter+Thug), [Voidwielder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Voidwielder) and Imp all unscathed. Leong summoned a [Centaur's Herald](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur%27s+Herald) and passed, his army severely reduced.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpsin13/GPSing-R5-Feature-Leong.jpg) *Whenever Leong looks at something that hard, it is most sure to die.* 
Ong regained what life he had lost off an attack with his Imp. Leong tried a [Rakdos's Return](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rakdos%27s+Return) to reclaim card parity, but Ong simply cast an overloaded [Street Spasm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Street+Spasm) and swing for the win next turn.


Calvin Ong 1 – Ding Leong 0


Leong started the second game with a [Korozda Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Korozda+Guildmage), while Ong had a [Frostburn Weird](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Frostburn+Weird). Leong followed with a [Daggerdrome Imp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daggerdrome+Imp), Ong keeping pace with an unleashed [Dead Reveler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dead+Reveler). On Leong's attack, Ong sighed and blocked the Guildmage, only to have the telegraphed [Giant Growth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Giant+Growth) take out his 1/4. A follow-up [Sewer Shambler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sewer+Shambler) kept the pressure on.


Ong had an [Annihilating Fire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Annihilating+Fire) for the [Sewer Shambler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sewer+Shambler), but was otherwise forced to take the damage from Leong's team as it marched in. Leong summoned an [Axebane Guardian](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Axebane+Guardian) and passed, while Ong summoned a [Rix Maadi Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rix+Maadi+Guildmage) and killed Leong's Guardian with an [Ultimate Price](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ultimate+Price).


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpsin13/GPSing-R5-Ong.jpg) *Ong has almost too many ways to win this game.* 
Leong attacked unblocked once more, knocking Ong to 13. Post-combat, he unleashed a [Dead Reveler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dead+Reveler). Ong untapped and cast a [Pursuit of Flight](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pursuit+of+Flight) on his Guildmage, swinging for 7. Tapped out and defenceless, Ong was helpless while Leong [Arrest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arrest)ed his Guildmage and attacked. The massive backswing in tempo was too much, and Ong succumbed a turn or two later.


Ding Leong 1 – Calvin Ong 1


Ong mulliganed to 5, Leong to 6, with Ong leading the action by unleashing a [Gore-House Chainwalker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gore-House+Chainwalker). Leong summoned a [Gatecreeper Vine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gatecreeper+Vine) and then found a [Dead Reveler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dead+Reveler), while Ong unleashed a [Splatter Thug](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splatter+Thug). The [Gatecreeper Vine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gatecreeper+Vine) blocked the Thug and then got all Grow-ey and Giant. Ong looked particularly unhappy about this, but had a [Stab Wound](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stab+Wound) after combat to soothe the pain of losing his Thug.


Leong summoned a [Sluiceway Scorpion](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sluiceway+Scorpion), while Ong cast a [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman). Leong attacked with his wounded Reveler, but Ong declined to block for some reason. With the [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) and the [Stab Wound](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stab+Wound) an effective clock on their own, all Ong had to do was sit back and wait for the win to arrive.


It wasn't long in coming.


**Calvin Ong 2 – Ding Leong 1**




Quick Questions – What is your deck's answer to s?
--------------------------------------------------


*by Event Coverage Staff*

 


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpsin13/QQ-Huang.jpg)***Hao-Shan Huang**: [Street Spasm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Street+Spasm) and [Ultimate Price](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ultimate+Price)*

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpsin13/QQ-Ang.jpg)***Ang Jun Yang**: [Stab Wound](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stab+Wound)*



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpsin13/QQ-Luo.jpg)***Ryan Luo**: [Dramatic Rescue](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dramatic+Rescue) then [Stab Wound](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stab+Wound)s* 

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpsin13/QQ-Chew.jpg)***Kelvin Chew**: [Auger Spree](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Auger+Spree)*




Round 5 Feature Match – Shuhei Nakamura vs. Martin Jůza
-------------------------------------------------------


*by Noel Neo*

 

This pairing was so clearly a feature match that Nakamura came up to our table before the feature match was even announced. Veteran pros and ChannelFireball teammates – Shuhei and Martin had prepared together during their byes and so were familiar with each others' decks. Despite the money on the line, the atmosphere was very casual; albeit the players' fame attracted quite the crowd of spectators.


Shuhei won the die roll and opted to play.


Game 1
------


Shuhei's early start of [Deviant Glee](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deviant+Glee) on [Gore-House Chainwalker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gore-House+Chainwalker) (unleashed) and [Daggerdrome Imp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daggerdrome+Imp) would taper off with Shuhei laying land after land...


On Martin's side of the table, [Drudge Beetle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Drudge+Beetle) and [Keening Apparition](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Keening+Apparition) worked to stem the bleeding, ganging up on the Gleeful Chainwalker, but not before he had dealt 6 points to the dome. [Selesnya Keyrune](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Selesnya+Keyrune) and [Dryad Militant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dryad+Militant) would join Martin's team, with [Towering Indrik](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Towering+Indrik) to fend off [Daggerdrome Imp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daggerdrome+Imp).


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpsin13/Shuhei-in-control-of-the-board.jpg) *Shuhei in control of the board.* 
[Tenement Crasher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tenement+Crasher) kept Shuhei in the game, with Martin summoning [Centaur Healer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur+Healer) and [Centaur's Herald](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur%27s+Herald) in response. Shuhei pushed his both his guys into the red zone and lost the Imp to [Towering Indrik](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Towering+Indrik) while his [Crash](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crash)er ate Martin's [Centaur Healer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur+Healer). [Spawn of Rix Maadi](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spawn+of+Rix+Maadi) replaced the Imp and Martin kept mana open for [Centaur's Herald](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur%27s+Herald).


On Shuhei's next attack, [Towering Indrik](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Towering+Indrik) and [Dryad Militant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dryad+Militant) ganged on the [Crash](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crash)er, which was great for Shuhei as [Annihilating Fire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Annihilating+Fire) took out the Dryad. Meanwhile, the Spawn's attack bounced off the Herald's ability.


On the other hand, Martin looked to be able to stabilize at 8 life, with [Voidwielder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Voidwielder) gaining a one turn tempo advantage and [Eyes in the Skies](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Eyes+in+the+Skies) for a bird and a centaur. However, the respite was only momentary as [Mizzium Mortars](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mizzium+Mortars) from Shuhei sealed the game.


Game 2
------


A quick one with Martin demonstrating he too could lay the beatdown. [New Prahv Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=New+Prahv+Guildmage) trumped [Rakdos Shred-Freak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rakdos+Shred-Freak) as it gained a [Common Bond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Common+Bond). Meanwhile [Daggerdrome Imp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daggerdrome+Imp) for Shuhei faced off against [Towering Indrik](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Towering+Indrik).


Shuhei sought to race with [Pursuit of Flight](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pursuit+of+Flight) on the Shred-Freak, but [Knightly Valor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knightly+Valor) on the Indrik brought Shuhei down to just 4 life. With Martin's creatures able to take flight with the Guildmage's ability, the game was quickly over.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpsin13/Martin-and-a-gathering-crowd.jpg) *Martin and a gathering crowd.* 
Game 3
------


Shuhei laid nothing but lands for the first 3 turns after his mulligan and the first creature to hit the board was Martin's [Centaur Healer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur+Healer), which immediately gained a [Stab Wound](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stab+Wound). Martin would build his team with [Skymark Roc](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Skymark+Roc), which made Shuhei's [Grim Roustabout](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grim+Roustabout) woefully ineffective.


A [Selesnya Keyrune](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Selesnya+Keyrune) and [Collective Blessing](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Collective+Blessing) later and it was all over.


**Final score: Martin Jůza 2 – Shuhei Nakamura 1**




Round 6 Feature Match – Sung-Wook Nam vs. Jun-Wei Hew
-----------------------------------------------------


*by Pip Foweraker*

 

Hew and Nam both led off their plays with a [Call of the Conclave](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Call+of+the+Conclave). Nam's follow-up was slightly more impressive: [Vitu-Ghazi Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vitu-Ghazi+Guildmage) when your opponent is also Selesnya, and thus predictably light on removal, makes for an attractive game indeed. Nonplussed, Hew summoned a [Keening Apparition](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Keening+Apparition).


Nam attacked with a pair of Centaur tokens. Hew had an [Eyes in the Skies](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Eyes+in+the+Skies) to net himself a Bird and another Centaur token. Post-combat, Nam summoned a [Golgari Longlegs](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Golgari+Longlegs).


The Longlegs attacked unblocked, and Hew had another [Eyes in the Skies](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Eyes+in+the+Skies) to keep his army a-growin', but declined to block. A [Deadbridge Goliath](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deadbridge+Goliath) gave Nam pause, and a follow-up [Collective Blessing](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Collective+Blessing) from Hew put Nam in an unpleasant spot indeed.


Hew attacked with a Centaur, his Goliath, and a Centaur. Before blockers, Nam had an [Eyes in the Skies](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Eyes+in+the+Skies) of his own, allowing him to block the Centaur, not block the Goliath, fall to 2, and see if his deck was going to give him any outs.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpsin13/GPSing-R6-Feature-Nam.jpg) *For a man taking approximately one bajillionty damage, Nam looks unfazed.* 
Waiting on top of Nam's library was a land – the 8th is not commonly important in Limited, but when you have a [Vitu-Ghazi Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vitu-Ghazi+Guildmage) on the board, it becomes very relevant indeed. Hew attacked with all the creatures that could. When the dust settled, Nam was left with a token and a Guildmage, and Hew had his Goliath and... an [Archon of the Triumvirate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Archon+of+the+Triumvirate). The Archon was detained by Nam's [Azorius Arrester](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Azorius+Arrester), and the Goliath rumbled in to tangle with the [Arrest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arrest)er. Post-combat, Hew cast an [Azorius Keyrune](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Azorius+Keyrune), leaving him with 2 fliers – enough to secure victory on the next turn.


Jun-Wei Hew 1 – Sung-Wook Nam 0


Neither player had anything for the first few turns of the game. A cautious [Centaur's Herald](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur%27s+Herald) from Hew was rapidly outclassed by a [Hussar Patrol](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hussar+Patrol), which suited up with a [Knightly Valor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knightly+Valor) and started bashing.


Hew cast a [Call of the Conclave](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Call+of+the+Conclave) and an [Azorius Arrester](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Azorius+Arrester) to get some early points of damage in. A [Dramatic Rescue](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dramatic+Rescue) on Nam's [Hussar Patrol](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hussar+Patrol) was countered with a [Dispel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dispel). When Nam attacked, Hew had an [Eyes in the Skies](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Eyes+in+the+Skies) and dramatically pushed a trio of Centaur tokens in front of the oncoming Hussar. An [Azorius Charm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Azorius+Charm) took care of one, but the Hussar bit the dust regardless.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpsin13/GPSing-R6-Feature-Hew.jpg) *Hew's plays are as dramatic as this photo's lighting.* 
The return swing from Hew was impressive, Nam left with a lonely 2/2 Knight on defense, who watched as the attackers sallied past. Nam summoned a [Vitu-Ghazi Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vitu-Ghazi+Guildmage). At the end of his turn, Hew had a [Druid's Deliverance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Druid%27s+Deliverance) to net himself another Centaur token, while Nam had an [Aerial Predation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aerial+Predation) to knock off the Bird.


Another attack from Hew saw no blocks from Nam, who cast a [Coursers' Accord](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Coursers%27+Accord) to shore up his defenses. When Hew attacked again, 4 Centaurs stared each other down in the red zone. Unfortunately for Nam, Hew's shared a [Common Bond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Common+Bond), and his [Arrest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arrest)er felt some [Swift Justice](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swift+Justice) and took down Nam's Knight.


Nam summoned an [Isperia's Skywatch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Isperia%27s+Skywatch), which detained a Centaur. Nam let the other Centaur crash in unheeded, needing something better to balance out the game. [Collective Blessing](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Collective+Blessing) was not the card he was hoping to see on his opponent's side of the board...


Or was it? On Hew's attack, Nam pulled out a [Sundering Growth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sundering+Growth), brushing off the troublesome enchantment and netting himself a Centaur to block the incoming army with. On a perilously low life total, Nam was forced to block with all his creatures, losing his Guildmage but stabilising with 2 blockers against a lone 4/4 Centaur.


Hew summoned a [Towering Indrik](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Towering+Indrik), while Nam had a [Call of the Conclave](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Call+of+the+Conclave). An [Eyes in the Skies](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Eyes+in+the+Skies) for Hew netted him a pair of Birds – enough to clinch the win past Nam's lonesome Skywatch.


**Jun-Wei Hew 2 – Sung-Wook Nam 0**




Round 7 Feature Match – Kelvin Chew vs. Hiew Chee Choong
--------------------------------------------------------


*by Noel Neo*

 

Kelvin is an emerging local pro who most recently made the top 8 at Pro Tour *Return to Ravnica* and led the Singapore contingent at Worlds 2012. He had earlier predicted that his deck would go x-2 and given his one loss with three rounds to go, it seems he might be right on target. Would this be the round where he picks up his second loss?


Chee Choong won the die roll and opted to play.


Game 1
------


Despite a mulligan on the play, Chee Choong managed to represent the stompy in this first game. A relatively mild [Security Blockade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Security+Blockade) met an unleashed [Dead Reveler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dead+Reveler) from Kelvin, and [Grove of the Guardian](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grove+of+the+Guardian) on turn four would portend how this game would play out.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpsin13/Kelvin-Chew-thinking-hard.jpg) *Kelvin Chew, thinking hard>.* 
Kelvin tried to ratchet up the pressure with [Viashino Racketeer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Viashino+Racketeer) (discarding [Sewer Shambler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sewer+Shambler)) and Chee Choong had end-of-turn [Eyes in the Skies](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Eyes+in+the+Skies) for a bird and knight. A Knight token traded with the Viashino and Chee Choong built his mana base with [Axebane Guardian](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Axebane+Guardian). The reason for the accelerator would be revealed the next turn as Chee Choong deployed [Risen Sanctuary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Risen+Sanctuary), far outstripping Kelvin's [Batterhorn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterhorn).


Kelvin mounted a valiant effort to take down the 8/8 vigilant elemental with a combination of [Batterhorn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Batterhorn) and [Auger Spree](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Auger+Spree). Whilst he represented some threat yet by scavenging [Sewer Shambler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sewer+Shambler) on [Dead Reveler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dead+Reveler) and adding [Bloodfray Giant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodfray+Giant), the game was all but over when Chee Choong cracked [Grove of the Guardian](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grove+of+the+Guardian) and played [Trostani's Judgment](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trostani%27s+Judgment) removing the Giant and populating his token.


Game 2
------


Kelvin Chew managed to get in some early beats with an unleashed [Grim Roustabout](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grim+Roustabout), while Chee Choong had an eye to the longer game with [Gatecreeper Vine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gatecreeper+Vine). Both side then upgraded with [Armory Guard](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Armory+Guard) for Chee Choong and [Golgari Longlegs](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Golgari+Longlegs) for Kelvin.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpsin13/Chee-Choong-with-Risen-Sanctuary-and-Grove-of-the-Guardian.jpg) *Chee Choong with [Risen Sanctuary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Risen+Sanctuary) and [Grove of the Guardian](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grove+of+the+Guardian).* 
Kelvin's lead would, however, be very brief as he had nary a response to Chee Choong's [Wayfaring Temple](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wayfaring+Temple) and [Coursers' Accord](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Coursers%27+Accord). Compounding his problems – Kelvin had been trying to push damage and when Chee Choong pushed his guys into the red zone, Kelvin could only [Ultimate Price](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ultimate+Price) the Guard, allowing [Wayfaring Temple](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wayfaring+Temple) to get through and populate.


[Sewer Shambler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sewer+Shambler) came down next for Kelvin, as Chee Choong presented his Vine for a chump block. Whilst Kelvin would subsequently be able to take down a [Palisade Giant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Palisade+Giant) and [Assassin's Strike](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Assassin%27s+Strike) Chee Choong's [Wayfaring Temple](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wayfaring+Temple), [Trostani's Judgment](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trostani%27s+Judgment) targeting [Golgari Longlegs](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Golgari+Longlegs) and populating a centaur would present too much board and card disadvantage for him to claw his way back from.


**Final score: Chee Choong 2 – Kelvin Chew 0**


In the aftermath of the brutally one-side match, Kelvin could only wonder at how good Chee Choong's deck was. Chee Choong explained that he had come into the event without any byes and had thus picked up his one and only loss partially because of the three additional matches he had to play.




Saturday, 7:25 p.m. – Sealed Deck Building Exercise #1: The Player
------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Noel Neo*

 

Earlier today, we showed you a Sealed pool and asked how you would build that deck. Our unnamed pro went with Rakdos for its suite of removal spells. Who is that player?


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpsin13/Kelvin-Chew-with-Jace-2.jpg) *Kelvin Chew* 
Kelvin Chew is one of Singapore's most dedicated professional players. When he's not helping out and honing his skills at games store – Games Haven, he spends hours working out the best strategies and decks to play on MTGO. His dedication has certainly paid off in spades, as evidenced by his making the top 8 at Pro Tour *Return to Ravnica* 2012 and leading the Singapore contingent at Worlds 2012.


"I chose to go with Rakdos for the suite of removal as well as the bomb in [Chaos Imps](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chaos+Imps)" Kelvin said. "Azorius has strong creatures, but I generally rate removal over creatures."


When pressed on why he is playing a sub-par card like [Cremate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cremate) main, Kelvin explained that his card pool was not so deep that he could play pure Rakdos without fillers. "I considered splashing green for cards such as [Gatecreeper Vine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gatecreeper+Vine) and [Savage Surge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Savage+Surge), but the marginal improvement in card quality is not worth sacrificing consistency for," Kelvin declared.


But how did things pan out for Kelvin? Well, that's a slightly different story. After eight rounds, Kelvin sat at a 5-3 record, needing a win in the final round and enough fortune with tie-breakers to make it into Day 2.


The losses he racked up were against perennially bad matchup – Selesnya, with its mix of life gain and fatter and more populous than Rakdos creatures, as well as a four color deck that played [Centaur Healer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur+Healer) and Sphinx's [Revelation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Revelation).


When asked if he would do anything differently if given a second shot, Kevin said he would board into a different deck against Selesnya – either Golgari splashing for removal or Azorius.




Round 8 Feature Match – Tzu-Ching Kuo vs. Jason Yeo
---------------------------------------------------


*by Noel Neo*

 

Kuo and Yeo both mulliganed, Yeo falling to 5, Kuo happy with his 6. Yeo had a [Seller of Songbirds](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Seller+of+Songbirds) to start play, while Kuo's first creature was a [Cobblebrute](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cobblebrute). Kuo summoned a [Lobber Crew](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lobber+Crew), and Yeo had a [Knightly Valor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knightly+Valor) for his Bird token, which swung over to nibble away at Kuo's life total.


Kuo built his army with an [Isperia's Skywatch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Isperia%27s+Skywatch). Yeo attacked with his Bird token, and Kuo blocked with his Skywatch. Yeo had a [Collective Blessing](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Collective+Blessing) to bring his flier up to a 5/5, and had a [Stab Wound](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stab+Wound) for Kuo's [Lobber Crew](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lobber+Crew) to add insult to injury. Kuo summoned a [Sphinx of the Chimes](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sphinx+of+the+Chimes), the 5/6 flier a perfect answer to Yeo's Bird.


Briefly stymied, Yeo summoned a [Korozda Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Korozda+Guildmage) and a [Concordia Pegasus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Concordia+Pegasus) before passing. Kuo had a second [Lobber Crew](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lobber+Crew), but his life was getting a little low. Yeo used his Guildmage to safely pump his Bird, before laying a second [Stab Wound](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stab+Wound) on the [Lobber Crew](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lobber+Crew). With Kuo taking 4 damage in his upkeep, it was time for sideboards.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpsin13/GPSing_R8_Feature_Yeo.jpg) *Yeo gets his Stab on.* 
Jason Yeo 1 – Tzu-Ching Kuo 0


Yeo had the first action of the second game, summoning a [Concordia Pegasus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Concordia+Pegasus). Kuo kept pace with a [Lobber Crew](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lobber+Crew) and a [Cobblebrute](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cobblebrute). A [Stab Wound](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stab+Wound) from Yeo got rid of the [Cobblebrute](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cobblebrute), and Kuo passed with 5 mana open. Yeo attacked with his Pegasus and also passed. At the end of his turn, Kuo fired off a [Thoughtflare](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtflare), getting an extra ping out of his Lobber and setting up his next turns.


Kuo cast a [Rakdos Keyrune](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rakdos+Keyrune) and passed with a full grip.. Yeo tried a [Deviant Glee](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deviant+Glee) on his Pegasus, which made the flying attacker far more impressive.


A [Voidwielder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Voidwielder) from Kuo dealt with both the Pegasus (for a turn) and the [Deviant Glee](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deviant+Glee) (more permanently). Kuo watched as Yeo summoned his Pegasus and followed it up with a [Korozda Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Korozda+Guildmage). Kuo killed the Guildmage with an [Izzet Charm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Izzet+Charm), then summoned a [Goblin Electromancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Electromancer). Yeo, stymied, summoned an [Angel of Serenity](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Angel+of+Serenity), but Kuo had a [Syncopate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Syncopate) for it. Sensing a window of opportunity, Kuo summoned a [Sphinx of the Chimes](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sphinx+of+the+Chimes) and began ring out some beats.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpsin13/GPSing_R8_Feature_Kuo.jpg) *Kuo refuses to Chime in with any puns about hand-wringing, dead ringers, or 'for whom the bell tolls' – despite them being so ap-pealing. Some people.* 
Yeo laid out a valiant defense, making the best of his pair of Pegasi and his [Trestle Troll](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Trestle+Troll), but failed to find anything relevant before dying a few turns later.


Tzu-Ching Kuo 1 – Jason Yeo 1


Kuo's deck betrayed him in the early turns of the final game. Kuo was forced to have crucial 3rd and 4th land drops come into play tapped and off-colour, stranding utility spells and creatures in hand while Yeo laid out threat after threat.


Kuo played a tight defensive game, maximising utility from a [Lobber Crew](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lobber+Crew) and some detain effects, but to no avail. Yeo simply kept pushing through, and by the time Kuo started to stabilise, it was too late.


**Jason Yeo – 2 Tzu-Ching Kuo 1**




Quick Questions – Your Favourite Preview Card?
----------------------------------------------


*by Pip Foweraker*

 


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpsin13/QQ-Ang.jpg)***Hao-Shan Huang**: Obzedat, Ghost Council*

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpsin13/QQ-Chew.jpg)***Kelvin Chew**: Lazav, Dimir Mastermind* 




Round 9 Feature Match – Stanislav Cifka vs. Choo Yong Han
---------------------------------------------------------


*by Noel Neo*

 

Fresh off his win last October at Pro Tour *Return to Ravnica*, Stanislav is looking to extend his streak here in Singapore. Standing in his way is Yong Han, a local pro with a Pro Tour top 8 and multiple Grand Prix top 8s. Both players are at 6 wins and need a win here to guarantee a spot in day 2.


Stanislav won the die roll and opted to play.


Game 1
------


Very quick game with Stanislav playing [Gatecreeper Vine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gatecreeper+Vine) into [Dreg Mangler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dreg+Mangler), into [Centaur Healer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur+Healer), into Bushstrider and [Sewer Shambler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sewer+Shambler).


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpsin13/Stanislav-happy-with-his-hand.jpg) *Stanislav, happy with his hand.* 
In contrast, Yong Han mulliganed into quartet of plains and could only mount a [Selesnya Sentry](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Selesnya+Sentry) to trade with [Dreg Mangler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dreg+Mangler) and a [Seller of Songbirds](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Seller+of+Songbirds) to trade with [Sewer Shambler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sewer+Shambler) (Stanislav had scavenged [Dreg Mangler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dreg+Mangler) on [Brushstrider](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Brushstrider) and Yong Han's Bird token could only chump block). He was soon overwhelmed by Stanislav's swarm.


Game 2
------


A very interesting game with unexpected twists and turns.


On the draw, Stanislav got the first play in with [Selesnya Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Selesnya+Guildmage). [Axebane Guardian](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Axebane+Guardian) did not block the following turn, perhaps playing around a possible [Common Bond](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Common+Bond); and Stanislav added to his board with [Seller of Songbirds](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Seller+of+Songbirds).


Yong Han summoned [Golgari Decoy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Golgari+Decoy), which promptly got [Ultimate Price](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ultimate+Price)'d, and Stanislav continued his beats. [Rogue's Passage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rogue%27s+Passage) and [Golgari Longlegs](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Golgari+Longlegs) for Yong Han managed to stem the bleeding as Stanislav could only add [Korozda Monitor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Korozda+Monitor) and swing with his Bird token.


The standoff continued for a couple more turns, with Yong Han adding [Collective Blessing](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Collective+Blessing) and [Dryad Militant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dryad+Militant) to his board. Things got interesting when Stanislav populated his Bird token, attacked Yong Han down to 12 life, and played [Stab Wound](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stab+Wound) on [Golgari Longlegs](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Golgari+Longlegs).


In a bad shape, Yong Han had an excellent response in an overloaded [Cyclonic Rift](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cyclonic+Rift) and swing to bring Stanislav down to 7 life. This, however, opened an opportunity for Stanislav to rush in with [Dreg Mangler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dreg+Mangler) + [Giant Growth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Giant+Growth) + [Swift Justice](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swift+Justice) to bring the life totals to Stanislav 14 – Yong Han 3. A valiant effort, but ultimately insufficient as Yong Han simply scavenged [Golgari Decoy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Golgari+Decoy) for the win.


Game 3
------


Stanislav mulliganed on the play and started on the back foot as a lone [Gatecreeper Vine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gatecreeper+Vine) faced [Centaur's Herald](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur%27s+Herald), [Drudge Beetle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Drudge+Beetle), and the centaur token off the Herald. Yong Han also had a [Grove of the Guardian](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grove+of+the+Guardian), which put some pressure on Stanislav to end the game quickly.


Stanislav got back into the game with [Selesnya Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Selesnya+Guildmage) and [Ultimate Price](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ultimate+Price) targeting the Centaur token, followed by [Centaur Healer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur+Healer) to bring himself back to 19 life. A clone of the [Heal](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Heal)er hit play on the opposite side, and Yong Han gang blocked the Guildmage on Stanislav's attack, [Swift Justice](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swift+Justice) and [Giant Growth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Giant+Growth) put Stanislav firmly in the driver'seat.


Another [Centaur Healer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur+Healer) for Yong Han met a second [Giant Growth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Giant+Growth) on the Guildmage, and Stanislav pushed further ahead with [Keening Apparition](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Keening+Apparition). Yong Han summoned [Seller of Songbirds](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Seller+of+Songbirds), and when Stanislav created a Centaur token via [Selesnya Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Selesnya+Guildmage), Trostani's *Judgment* took out the Guildmage and created a Bird token for Yong Han.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gpsin13/Yong-Han-mulling-his-blocks.jpg) *Yong Han mulling his blocks.* 
The following turn saw [Seller of Songbirds](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Seller+of+Songbirds) and token gang block the Apparition (Stanislav chose to take out the token), and Stanislav added [Centaur's Herald](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur%27s+Herald), which he promptly cracked. Yong Han had [Dryad Militant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dryad+Militant), which made for an excellent defense step when he played [Rootborn Defenses](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rootborn+Defenses) (populating a bird) to stonewall Stanislav's attack and kill his [Centaur Healer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur+Healer) (leaving Stanislav with two 3/3 centaur tokens). Yong Han then attacked with both Bird tokens and stabilized the board with [Centaur Healer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Centaur+Healer) to bring himself back up to 12 life.


With the ground now gummed up, Yong Han continued to chip away with his birds and added Trostani, Selesnya's Voice to take the game and match.


Final score: Choo Yong Han 2 – Stanislav Cifka 1
